- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

{"content":"1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference pa
... (truncated)

     1→# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide
     2→## v1.30.0 → v1.31.0
     3→
     4→---
     5→
     6→## 1. Overview
     7→
     8→The Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter migration from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0 introduces several important improvements focused on:
     9→
    10→- **Route Cache Control**: Enhanced route cache handling with an enum-based approach replacing the boolean flag
    11→- **Observability Mode Enhancements**: Improved support for observing HTTP traffic without affecting request/response flow
    12→- **Stream Lifecycle Management**: Better control over gRPC stream closure, especially in observability mode
    13→- **Deferred Stream Closure**: New mechanism to properly defer external processor stream closure with configurable timeout
    14→
    15→This migration is relatively non-disruptive, but involves configuration changes and behavioral updates for users relying on route cache controls and observability mode.
    16→
    17→---
    18→
    19→## 2. Breaking Changes
    20→
    21→### 2.1 Route Cache Control Behavior
    22→
    23→**Impact Level**: HIGH - Configuration change required
    24→
    25→In v1.30, route cache control was a simple boolean:
    26→```protobuf
    27→// v1.30 - ext_proc.proto
    28→bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;
    29→```
    30→
    31→In v1.31, this has been replaced with an enum-based approach:
    32→```protobuf
    33→// v1.31 - ext_proc.proto
    34→enum RouteCacheAction {
    35→  DEFAULT = 0;   // Default: clear cache when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache
    36→  CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear route cache
    37→  RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear route cache
    38→}
    39→
    40→// Only one of these can be set:
    41→bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;      // Dep

### Key Sections Included:

1. **Overview** - High-level summary of major changes (route cache control, observability enhancements, stream lifecycle)

2. **Breaking Changes** - Two critical changes:

    "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n12: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n15: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n16: \n17: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n18: option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n19: option java_multiple_files = true;\n20: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n22: \n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n24: // External Processing Filter\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n26: \n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n28: \n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n31: //\n32: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n33: \n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n36: //\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n41: //\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n44: // and how it should be processed.\n45: //\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n47: //\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n53: //\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\n57: //\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n63: //   to SEND.\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n69: //   request trailers.\n70: //\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n78: //\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n81: //\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n89: //\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n91: // server\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n95: //\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n98: // name.\n99: //\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\n102:   reserved 4;\n103: \n104:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n105: \n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n107:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n109: \n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\\n118:     // to true.\\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\\n120:   }\\n121: \\n122:   reserved 4;\\n123: \\n124:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n125: \\n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n127:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n129: \\n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n141:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n142: \n143:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n144:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n145:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n146:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n147:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n148:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n149: \n150:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n151:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n152:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n153:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n154:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n155:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n156: \n157:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n158:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n159:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n160:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n161:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n164:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n165:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n166:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n167:     gte {}\n168:   }];\n169: \n170:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n176:   // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n177:   // with the header prefix set via\n178:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n179:   // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n180:   // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n181:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. The metadata\n200:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n201:   // ext_proc filter name.\n202:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n203: \n204:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n205:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n206:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n207:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n208:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n209:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n210: \n211:   // If set to true, ignore the\n212:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n213:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n214:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n215:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n216:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n217: \n218:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n219:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n220: \n221:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n222:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n223:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n224:   //\n225:   // 1. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n227:   //\n228:   // 2. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n27:     // while trailers are skipped.\n28:     DEFAULT = 0;\n29: \n30:     // Send the header or trailer.\n31:     SEND = 1;\n32: \n33:     // Do not send the header or trailer.\n34:     SKIP = 2;\n35:   }\n36: \n37:   // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n38:   // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n39:   // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n40:   // to be set correctly:\n41:   // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n42:   // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n43:   // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n44:   //\n45:   // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n46:   // encoding whenever feasible.   "content": "{\"content\":\"1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\\n2: \\n3: External Processing\\n4: ===================\\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\\n7: \\n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \\\"external processor,\\\"\\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\\n37: \\n38: The following statistics are supported:\\n39: \\n40: .. csv-table::\\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\\n42:   :widths: auto\\n43: \\n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\\n55: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--50ea83e6@1ee8aa56b83277e4f804bb70a12461d54ad68fa5/-/blob/docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst\"}",
  "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n30: \n31: Statistics\n32: ----------\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n37: \n38: The following statistics are supported:\n39: \n40: .. csv-table::\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\n42:   :widths: auto\n43: \n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n55: ",

{
  "content": "# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide\n## v1.30.0 \u2192 v1.31.0\n\n---\n\n## 1. Overview\n\nThe Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter migration from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0 introduces several important improvements focused on:\n\n- **Route Cache Control**: Enhanced route cache handling with an enum-based approach replacing the boolean flag\n- **Observability Mode Enhancements**: Improved support for observing HTTP traffic without affecting request/response flow\n- **Stream Lifecycle Management**: Better control over gRPC stream closure, especially in observability mode\n- **Deferred Stream Closure**: New mechanism to properly defer external processor stream closure with configurable timeout\n\nThis migration is relatively non-disruptive, but involves configuration changes and behavioral updates for users relying on route cache controls and observability mode.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Control Behavior\n\n**Impact Level**: HIGH - Configuration change required\n\nIn v1.30, route cache control was a simple boolean:\n```protobuf\n// v1.30 - ext_proc.proto\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\nIn v1.31, this has been replaced with an enum-based approach:\n```protobuf\n// v1.31 - ext_proc.proto\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  DEFAULT = 0;   // Default: clear cache when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache\n  CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear route cache\n  RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear route cache\n}\n\n// Only one of these can be set:\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;      // Deprecated (marked for migration)\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18; // New preferred field\n```\n\n**Migration Required**:\n- **If you set `disable_clear_route_cache: true`** \u2192 Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- **If you didn't set it (or set false)** \u2192 Use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n\n**Before (v1.30)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Prevents route cache clearing\n```\n\n**After (v1.31)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Same behavior, new enum\n```\n\n**Key Behavioral Differences**:\n- `DEFAULT` (new): Allows external processor to control route cache via `clear_route_cache` field\n- `CLEAR`: Always clears route cache, overriding ext_proc response settings\n- `RETAIN`: Never clears route cache, equivalent to old `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n### 2.2 Stream Pointer Management\n\n**Impact Level**: INTERNAL - Only affects custom filter implementations\n\nThe internal stream pointer management has changed in the Filter class:\n- **v1.30**: `ExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_` (unique_ptr)\n- **v1.31**: `ExternalProcessorStream* stream_` (raw pointer) + ThreadLocalStreamManager\n\nThis change enables deferred stream closure in observability mode. Standard users relying on the public API won't be affected.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Field\n\n**Status**: Deprecated (not yet removed, but superseded)\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11) is deprecated in favor of the new `route_cache_action` enum (field 18).\n\n**Timeline**:\n- **v1.31**: Both fields available, but `route_cache_action` is recommended\n- **v1.32+**: `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed\n\n**Migration Advice**:\nUpdate your configuration to use `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions:\n```yaml\n# Deprecated pattern (still works but not recommended)\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# Recommended pattern\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Important**: Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` should be set. The oneof field promotion in the proto ensures this constraint.\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 Enhanced Route Cache Control with `route_cache_action`\n\n**Field**: `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type**: `RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nProvides three distinct strategies for handling route cache:\n\n#### Option 1: DEFAULT (Value: 0)\nAllows the external processor to control route cache clearing via the `clear_route_cache` field in `ProcessingResponse`.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You want the external processor to decide whether to clear the route cache based on header modifications or other factors.\n\n#### Option 2: CLEAR (Value: 1)\nAlways clears the route cache after external processor response, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Use Case**: External processing always modifies routing-relevant headers, so caching should be disabled.\n\n#### Option 3: RETAIN (Value: 2)\nNever clears the route cache, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` requests from the external processor.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You've verified that external processing never affects routing decisions, and want to avoid the performance cost of cache invalidation.\n\n### 4.2 Deferred Stream Closure for Observability Mode\n\n**Field**: `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19)\n**Type**: `google.protobuf.Duration`\n**Default**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nIn observability mode, external processor streams are decoupled from the main HTTP request/response lifecycle. The `deferred_close_timeout` controls how long these streams remain open after the HTTP transaction completes.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 10  # Keep stream open for up to 10 seconds\n```\n\n**Internal Implementation**:\n- **New Classes**: `DeferredDeletableStream` and `ThreadLocalStreamManager`\n- **Mechanism**: Streams are queued for deferred closure instead of being immediately deleted\n- **Cleanup**: A timeout timer ensures streams don't persist indefinitely\n\n**Behavioral Changes in Observability Mode**:\n\nIn v1.30, observability mode had limited deferred closure support. v1.31 adds:\n- Configurable deferred closure timeout\n- Proper stream lifecycle management\n- Thread-safe stream tracking via ThreadLocalStreamManager\n- Timeout-based cleanup to prevent resource exhaustion\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: observability_processor\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 30  # Wait up to 30 seconds before closing stream\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### 4.3 Observability Mode Enhancements\n\n**Updated Features**:\n- Added `encodeComplete()` hook to ensure logging happens after entire response is sent\n- New `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` method for better header handling\n- New `sendDataInObservabilityMode()` method for body streaming without blocking\n- Enhanced `sendTrailers()` with observability mode awareness\n- New `buildHeaderRequest()` method supporting observability mode flag\n\n**Impact**:\nUsers enabling observability mode will benefit from:\n- Better separation of observability streams from request/response flow\n- Improved performance by not pausing filter chain execution\n- More robust timeout handling for external processor streams\n\n---\n\n## 5. Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Assess Current Configuration\n\nIdentify all ext_proc filter configurations:\n\n```bash\n# Find all references to ext_proc in your Envoy configs\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\" /path/to/configs/\n```\n\nCheck if you use:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache` field\n- `observability_mode` field\n\n### Step 2: Update Route Cache Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf your configuration uses route cache control:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Old way\n```\n\n**Migrate to v1.31**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # New way - equivalent behavior\n```\n\n**Decision Matrix**:\n\n| v1.30 Setting | v1.31 Equivalent | When to Use |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Processor controls cache clearing |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Processor never affects routing |\n| N/A | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Processor always affects routing |\n\n### Step 3: Update Observability Mode Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf you use observability mode, explicitly configure the deferred close timeout:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration** (implicit default):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n```\n\n**v1.31 Configuration** (explicit timeout):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout:\n      seconds: 5  # Explicitly set timeout (default is 5 seconds)\n```\n\n**Timeout Considerations**:\n- **Default (5 seconds)**: Good for most use cases, minimal memory overhead\n- **Longer timeout (10-30 seconds)**: For processors that need more time to flush data\n- **Shorter timeout (1-2 seconds)**: When memory is constrained, accept occasional stream interruptions\n\n### Step 4: Validate Proto Compatibility\n\nBefore deployment, verify your config validates against the new proto:\n\n```bash\n# Using envoy CLI (if available)\nenvoy -c config.yaml --mode validate\n\n# Or use protoc to validate\nprotoc --validate_out=/tmp ext_proc_config.textproto\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test in Staging Environment\n\n1. Deploy v1.31 Envoy with updated configuration\n2. Verify ext_proc filter still processes requests correctly\n3. Check that route cache behavior matches expectations\n4. Monitor observability processor stream lifecycle (if using observability mode)\n\n**Key Tests**:\n- Route mutation behavior unchanged\n- Route cache clearing works as expected (use `CLEAR`, `DEFAULT`, or `RETAIN`)\n- Observability mode streams close properly and don't accumulate\n\n### Step 6: Deploy to Production\n\nOnce validated in staging:\n\n```bash\n# Gradual rollout recommended\ncanary_deployment(envoy_v1.31, percentage=10)\nmonitor_metrics()\nif errors_acceptable:\n  full_deployment(envoy_v1.31)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 6.1 Unit Testing\n\nCreate tests to verify route cache behavior:\n\n```python\n# Pseudocode for test cases\ntest_route_cache_action_default():\n  # Processor's clear_route_cache field should control cache clearing\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert route_cache_cleared()\n\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()\n\ntest_route_cache_action_clear():\n  # Cache should always be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert route_cache_cleared()  # Still cleared!\n\ntest_route_cache_action_retain():\n  # Cache should never be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()  # Still retained!\n\ntest_deferred_close_timeout():\n  # In observability mode, streams should close after timeout\n  enable_observability_mode()\n  set_deferred_close_timeout(seconds=1)\n\n  send_request()\n  assert_stream_open()\n\n  wait(milliseconds=1100)\n  assert_stream_closed()\n```\n\n### 6.2 Integration Testing\n\nTest with actual ext_proc processor:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Deploy test ext_proc service\ndocker run -d test_ext_proc_service\n\n# 2. Test route cache clearing behavior\ncurl http://envoy:10000/api/test-route-cache \\\n  -H \"X-Modify-Route-Header: true\"\n\n# Verify: Route cache behavior matches configuration\n\n# 3. Test observability mode (if enabled)\ncurl http://envoy:10000/api/test-observability\n\n# Verify:\n# - Request completes immediately\n# - Processor stream stays open for configured timeout\n# - No stream accumulation over time\n```\n\n### 6.3 Performance Testing\n\nCompare v1.30 vs v1.31 under load:\n\n**Metrics to Monitor**:\n- Request latency (should be identical)\n- Memory usage (especially in observability mode)\n- gRPC stream count (should stabilize around expected number)\n- Route cache hit rate (shouldn't change)\n\n**Load Test Scenario**:\n```\n- Concurrent requests: 1000\n- Request rate: 10,000 req/s\n- Duration: 5 minutes\n- Observability mode: enabled with 5s timeout\n```\n\nExpected Results:\n- Latency: \u00b15% of v1.30\n- Memory: Similar to v1.30 (deferred streams are temporary)\n- Streams: Should match concurrent request count + observability overhead\n\n---\n\n## 7. Rollback Guidance\n\n### 7.1 Quick Rollback (If Issues Occur)\n\nIf you experience problems after upgrading:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Revert Envoy to v1.30\ndeploy_envoy(version=1.30.0)\n\n# 2. Revert configuration\nrevert_config(git_commit=last_working)\n\n# 3. Restart proxies\nrestart_envoy_instances()\n```\n\n**Rollback Time Estimate**: < 5 minutes (depending on deployment infrastructure)\n\n### 7.2 Configuration-Only Rollback\n\nIf only configuration changes cause issues:\n\n```yaml\n# From v1.31 (problematic)\nroute_cache_action: CLEAR\ndeferred_close_timeout:\n  seconds: 30\n\n# Rolled back to v1.30-compatible\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true  # Equivalent to RETAIN\n# deferred_close_timeout removed (not supported in v1.30)\n```\n\n### 7.3 Safe Rollback Procedure\n\n1. **Identify the issue** via logs and metrics\n2. **Test rollback in staging** first\n3. **Prepare rollback config** with v1.30 format\n4. **Execute gradual rollback** (don't do all at once)\n5. **Monitor for stability** before considering it complete\n\n**Critical Monitoring During Rollback**:\n- Request error rates (should drop if ext_proc was the cause)\n- Route cache hit rates (should stabilize)\n- gRPC stream errors\n- Memory usage\n\n---\n\n## 8. Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n### Pitfall 1: Setting Both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflicting!\n```\n\n**Result**: One field takes precedence (undefined behavior depending on proto implementation)\n\n**Solution**: Use only `route_cache_action` in v1.31:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Clear choice\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Forgetting to Configure `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n**Problem**: Without explicit timeout configuration, default behavior applies but may not match your expectations.\n\n**Solution**: Be explicit:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Make it clear this is intentional\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Incorrect Route Cache Action Choice\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\n# Wrong: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Processor decides to clear (slower)\n```\n\n**Solution**: Match action to your processor's behavior:\n```yaml\n# Right: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear for correctness\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Observability Mode Without Resource Limits\n\n**Problem**: Deferred streams in observability mode can accumulate if:\n- `deferred_close_timeout` is too long\n- External processor is slow to acknowledge\n- High request volume with many concurrent streams\n\n**Solution**: Monitor and tune:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Keep it reasonable (default is good)\n  # Consider separate resource limits for observability streams\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Compatibility Matrix\n\n| Feature | v1.30 | v1.31 | Backward Compat |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Basic ext_proc functionality | \u2713 | \u2713 | Full |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | \u2713 | \u2713* | Deprecated |\n| `route_cache_action` | \u2717 | \u2713 | N/A |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | \u2717 | \u2713 | N/A |\n| Observability mode | \u2713 | \u2713\u2020 | Enhanced |\n| Processing modes | \u2713 | \u2713 | Full |\n| Metadata options | \u2713 | \u2713 | Full |\n| Header mutation rules | \u2713 | \u2713 | Full |\n\n**Legend**:\n- \u2713 = Supported\n- \u2717 = Not supported\n- \u2713* = Supported but deprecated\n- \u2713\u2020 = Supported with enhancements\n\n---\n\n## 10. Version-Specific Configuration Examples\n\n### Complete v1.30 Configuration\n\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: ext_proc_service\n  connect_timeout: 2s\n  type: STRICT_DNS\n  lb_policy: ROUND_ROBIN\n  load_assignment:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    endpoints:\n    - lb_endpoints:\n      - endpoint:\n          address:\n            socket_address:\n              address: 127.0.0.1\n              port_value: 50051\n\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    failure_mode_allow: false\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n      request_body_mode: BUFFERED\n      response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### Equivalent v1.31 Configuration\n\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: ext_proc_service\n  connect_timeout: 2s\n  type: STRICT_DNS\n  lb_policy: ROUND_ROBIN\n  load_assignment:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    endpoints:\n    - lb_endpoints:\n      - endpoint:\n          address:\n            socket_address:\n              address: 127.0.0.1\n              port_value: 50051\n\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    failure_mode_allow: false\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # NEW: replaces disable_clear_route_cache\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n      request_body_mode: BUFFERED\n      response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### v1.31 with Observability Mode and Deferred Closure\n\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: ext_proc_service\n  connect_timeout: 2s\n  type: STRICT_DNS\n  lb_policy: ROUND_ROBIN\n  load_assignment:\n    cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    endpoints:\n    - lb_endpoints:\n      - endpoint:\n          address:\n            socket_address:\n              address: 127.0.0.1\n              port_value: 50051\n\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    failure_mode_allow: true\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # NEW: allows processor to control\n    observability_mode: true  # NEW: don't block request/response\n    deferred_close_timeout:\n      seconds: 10  # NEW: wait 10s before closing observability stream\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      request_body_mode: STREAMED\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n      response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n---\n\n## 11. Reference: Proto Changes Detail\n\n### Imports Added\n```protobuf\n// Added in v1.31\nimport \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n```\n\n### New Enum\n```protobuf\n// New in v1.31 (field 102-120)\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Protobuf comment: The default behavior is to clear the route cache\n  // only when the clear_route_cache field is set in the external\n  // processor response.\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is\n  // equivalent to setting disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n### Field Changes\n```protobuf\n// v1.30\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n// v1.31 - with deprecation migration annotation\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n// v1.31 - new field\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n// v1.31 - new field\ngoogle.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n```\n\n---\n\n## 12. Frequently Asked Questions\n\n### Q: Do I have to update my configuration immediately?\n\n**A**: No. Both configurations work in v1.31, but we recommend updating to `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions where `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed.\n\n### Q: What happens if I don't set `route_cache_action`?\n\n**A**: It defaults to `DEFAULT`, which means the external processor can control route cache clearing. This matches the behavior of `disable_clear_route_cache: false` in v1.30.\n\n### Q: Does deferred_close_timeout affect request latency?\n\n**A**: No. The timeout only applies to the external processor stream in observability mode, after the HTTP response is complete. It doesn't affect request/response processing.\n\n### Q: Can I still use `disable_clear_route_cache` in v1.31?\n\n**A**: Yes, but it's deprecated. Prefer `route_cache_action` for clarity and future compatibility.\n\n### Q: What's the performance impact of v1.31?\n\n**A**: Negligible for non-observability-mode deployments. Observability mode may use slightly more memory due to deferred stream management, but this is temporary and controlled by timeout.\n\n### Q: How do I know which `route_cache_action` to use?\n\n**A**:\n- Use `DEFAULT` if your external processor sometimes modifies routing headers\n- Use `CLEAR` if your external processor always modifies routing headers\n- Use `RETAIN` if your external processor never modifies routing headers\n\n---\n\n## 13. Support and Troubleshooting\n\n### Common Issues\n\n**Issue**: Route cache not clearing as expected after upgrade\n**Solution**: Check that you're using `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` or `CLEAR`, not `RETAIN`\n\n**Issue**: Observability mode streams accumulating\n**Solution**: Lower `deferred_close_timeout` or check if external processor is hanging\n\n**Issue**: Configuration validation fails after upgrade\n**Solution**: Ensure you're not setting both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n\n### Getting Help\n\n1.   "content": "# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide\n## v1.30.0 \u2192 v1.31.0\n\n---\n\n## 1. Overview\n\nThe Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter migration from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0 introduces several important improvements focused on:\n\n- **Route Cache Control**: Enhanced route cache handling with an enum-based approach replacing the boolean flag\n- **Observability Mode Enhancements**: Improved support for observing HTTP traffic without affecting request/response flow\n- **Stream Lifecycle Management**: Better control over gRPC stream closure, especially in observability mode\n- **Deferred Stream Closure**: New mechanism to properly defer external processor stream closure with configurable timeout\n\nThis migration is relatively non-disruptive, but involves configuration changes and behavioral updates for users relying on route cache controls and observability mode.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Control Behavior\n\n**Impact Level**: HIGH - Configuration change required\n\nIn v1.30, route cache control was a simple boolean:\n```protobuf\n// v1.30 - ext_proc.proto\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\nIn v1.31, this has been replaced with an enum-based approach:\n```protobuf\n// v1.31 - ext_proc.proto\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  DEFAULT = 0;   // Default: clear cache when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache\n  CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear route cache\n  RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear route cache\n}\n\n// Only one of these can be set:\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;      // Deprecated (marked for migration)\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18; // New preferred field\n```\n\n**Migration Required**:\n- **If you set `disable_clear_route_cache: true`** \u2192 Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- **If you didn't set it (or set false)** \u2192 Use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n\n**Before (v1.30)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Prevents route cache clearing\n```\n\n**After (v1.31)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Same behavior, new enum\n```\n\n**Key Behavioral Differences**:\n- `DEFAULT` (new): Allows external processor to control route cache via `clear_route_cache` field\n- `CLEAR`: Always clears route cache, overriding ext_proc response settings\n- `RETAIN`: Never clears route cache, equivalent to old `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n### 2.2 Stream Pointer Management\n\n**Impact Level**: INTERNAL - Only affects custom filter implementations\n\nThe internal stream pointer management has changed in the Filter class:\n- **v1.30**: `ExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_` (unique_ptr)\n- **v1.31**: `ExternalProcessorStream* stream_` (raw pointer) + ThreadLocalStreamManager\n\nThis change enables deferred stream closure in observability mode. Standard users relying on the public API won't be affected.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Field\n\n**Status**: Deprecated (not yet removed, but superseded)\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11) is deprecated in favor of the new `route_cache_action` enum (field 18).\n\n**Timeline**:\n- **v1.31**: Both fields available, but `route_cache_action` is recommended\n- **v1.32+**: `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed\n\n**Migration Advice**:\nUpdate your configuration to use `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions:\n```yaml\n# Deprecated pattern (still works but not recommended)\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# Recommended pattern\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Important**: Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` should be set. The oneof field promotion in the proto ensures this constraint.\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 Enhanced Route Cache Control with `route_cache_action`\n\n**Field**: `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type**: `RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nProvides three distinct strategies for handling route cache:\n\n#### Option 1: DEFAULT (Value: 0)\nAllows the external processor to control route cache clearing via the `clear_route_cache` field in `ProcessingResponse`.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You want the external processor to decide whether to clear the route cache based on header modifications or other factors.\n\n#### Option 2: CLEAR (Value: 1)\nAlways clears the route cache after external processor response, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Use Case**: External processing always modifies routing-relevant headers, so caching should be disabled.\n\n#### Option 3: RETAIN (Value: 2)\nNever clears the route cache, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` requests from the external processor.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You've verified that external processing never affects routing decisions, and want to avoid the performance cost of cache invalidation.\n\n### 4.2 Deferred Stream Closure for Observability Mode\n\n**Field**: `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19)\n**Type**: `google.protobuf.Duration`\n**Default**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nIn observability mode, external processor streams are decoupled from the main HTTP request/response lifecycle. The `deferred_close_timeout` controls how long these streams remain open after the HTTP transaction completes.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 10  # Keep stream open for up to 10 seconds\n```\n\n**Internal Implementation**:\n- **New Classes**: `DeferredDeletableStream` and `ThreadLocalStreamManager`\n- **Mechanism**: Streams are queued for deferred closure instead of being immediately deleted\n- **Cleanup**: A timeout timer ensures streams don't persist indefinitely\n\n**Behavioral Changes in Observability Mode**:\n\nIn v1.30, observability mode had limited deferred closure support. v1.31 adds:\n- Configurable deferred closure timeout\n- Proper stream lifecycle management\n- Thread-safe stream tracking via ThreadLocalStreamManager\n- Timeout-based cleanup to prevent resource exhaustion\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: observability_processor\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 30  # Wait up to 30 seconds before closing stream\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### 4.3 Observability Mode Enhancements\n\n**Updated Features**:\n- Added `encodeComplete()` hook to ensure logging happens after entire response is sent\n- New `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` method for better header handling\n- New `sendDataInObservabilityMode()` method for body streaming without blocking\n- Enhanced `sendTrailers()` with observability mode awareness\n- New `buildHeaderRequest()` method supporting observability mode flag\n\n**Impact**:\nUsers enabling observability mode will benefit from:\n- Better separation of observability streams from request/response flow\n- Improved performance by not pausing filter chain execution\n- More robust timeout handling for external processor streams\n\n---\n\n## 5. Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Assess Current Configuration\n\nIdentify all ext_proc filter configurations:\n\n```bash\n# Find all references to ext_proc in your Envoy configs\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\" /path/to/configs/\n```\n\nCheck if you use:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache` field\n- `observability_mode` field\n\n### Step 2: Update Route Cache Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf your configuration uses route cache control:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Old way\n```\n\n**Migrate to v1.31**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # New way - equivalent behavior\n```\n\n**Decision Matrix**:\n\n| v1.30 Setting | v1.31 Equivalent | When to Use |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Processor controls cache clearing |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Processor never affects routing |\n| N/A | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Processor always affects routing |\n\n### Step 3: Update Observability Mode Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf you use observability mode, explicitly configure the deferred close timeout:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration** (implicit default):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n```\n\n**v1.31 Configuration** (explicit timeout):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout:\n      seconds: 5  # Explicitly set timeout (default is 5 seconds)\n```\n\n**Timeout Considerations**:\n- **Default (5 seconds)**: Good for most use cases, minimal memory overhead\n- **Longer timeout (10-30 seconds)**: For processors that need more time to flush data\n- **Shorter timeout (1-2 seconds)**: When memory is constrained, accept occasional stream interruptions\n\n### Step 4: Validate Proto Compatibility\n\nBefore deployment, verify your config validates against the new proto:\n\n```bash\n# Using envoy CLI (if available)\nenvoy -c config.yaml --mode validate\n\n# Or use protoc to validate\nprotoc --validate_out=/tmp ext_proc_config.textproto\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test in Staging Environment\n\n1. Deploy v1.31 Envoy with updated configuration\n2. Verify ext_proc filter still processes requests correctly\n3. Check that route cache behavior matches expectations\n4. Monitor observability processor stream lifecycle (if using observability mode)\n\n**Key Tests**:\n- Route mutation behavior unchanged\n- Route cache clearing works as expected (use `CLEAR`, `DEFAULT`, or `RETAIN`)\n- Observability mode streams close properly and don't accumulate\n\n### Step 6: Deploy to Production\n\nOnce validated in staging:\n\n```bash\n# Gradual rollout recommended\ncanary_deployment(envoy_v1.31, percentage=10)\nmonitor_metrics()\nif errors_acceptable:\n  full_deployment(envoy_v1.31)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 6.1 Unit Testing\n\nCreate tests to verify route cache behavior:\n\n```python\n# Pseudocode for test cases\ntest_route_cache_action_default():\n  # Processor's clear_route_cache field should control cache clearing\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert route_cache_cleared()\n\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()\n\ntest_route_cache_action_clear():\n  # Cache should always be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert route_cache_cleared()  # Still cleared!\n\ntest_route_cache_action_retain():\n  # Cache should never be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()  # Still retained!\n\ntest_deferred_close_timeout():\n  # In observability mode, streams should close after timeout\n  enable_observability_mode()\n  set_deferred_close_timeout(seconds=1)\n\n  send_request()\n  assert_stream_open()\n\n  wait(milliseconds=1100)\n  assert_stream_closed()\n```\n\n### 6.2 Integration Testing\n\nTest with actual ext_proc processor:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n### Pitfall 1: Setting Both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflicting!\n```\n\n**Result**: One field takes precedence (undefined behavior depending on proto implementation)\n\n**Solution**: Use only `route_cache_action` in v1.31:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Clear choice\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Forgetting to Configure `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n**Problem**: Without explicit timeout configuration, default behavior applies but may not match your expectations.\n\n**Solution**: Be explicit:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Make it clear this is intentional\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Incorrect Route Cache Action Choice\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\n# Wrong: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Processor decides to clear (slower)\n```\n\n**Solution**: Match action to your processor's behavior:\n```yaml\n# Right: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear for correctness\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Observability Mode Without Resource Limits\n\n**Problem**: Deferred streams in observability mode can accumulate if:\n- `deferred_close_timeout` is too long\n- External processor is slow to acknowledge\n- High request volume with many concurrent streams\n\n**Solution**: Monitor and tune:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Keep it reasonable (default is good)\n  # Consider separate resource limits for observability streams\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9.
